Two Stage Admission Process - to allow external controllers to co-decide about workload admission.

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:102** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-08-04T17:49:18Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,226 @@
+# KEP-993: Two Stage Admission Process
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)](#notesconstraintscaveats-optional)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP defines the extension point to plug in arbitrary, additional checks
+for workloads before they are admitted for execution. These external checks may
+be implemented inside or outside of Kueue and may provide functionality like
+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.
+
+## Motivation
+
+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, each
+reflecting the go/no-go decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
```

  ```suggestion
  	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"admissionChecks"`
  ```

+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
```

  State whether the order of the list is relevant to kueue.

+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)

+
+## Summary

+be established.

+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the

+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly

+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry CheckFailureState = “Retry”
+	Reject CheckFailureState = “Reject”
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check.
```

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:154** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-08-04T18:07:17Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,226 @@
+# KEP-993: Two Stage Admission Process
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)](#notesconstraintscaveats-optional)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP defines the extension point to plug in arbitrary, additional checks
+for workloads before they are admitted for execution. These external checks may
+be implemented inside or outside of Kueue and may provide functionality like
+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.
+
+## Motivation
+
+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, each
+reflecting the go/no-go decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry CheckFailureState = “Retry”
+	Reject CheckFailureState = “Reject”
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check.
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+// Points to where the parameters for the checks are. 
+// As clusterqueue are in cluster scope - this should be
+// a dedicated CRD specific for the Controller.
+type AdmissionCheckParametersReference struct {
+	// ApiGroup is the group for the resource being referenced. 
+	APIGroup string `json:"apiGroup"`
+
+	// Kind is the type of the resource being referenced.
+	Kind string `json:"kind""`
+
+	// Name is the name of the resource being referenced.
+	Name string `json:"name"`
+}
+```
+
+For every workload that is put to a ClusterQueue, Kueue will perform the very 
+same checks that it does today, before admitting a workload. However, once the basic checks pass AND there are some AdmissionChecks configured, AND the workload is not in on-hold retry state from some check, it will:
+
+1. Fill the Admission field in workload, with the desired flavor assignment. 
+2. Not do any preemptions yet.
+3. Set conditions on the workload:
+* “AdmissionPrecheck” to true
+* “AdmissionCheck|<checkName>” to unknown for each of the add
```

  Validation here might be tricky:
  `checkName` has to be a valid CRD name. Whereas the condition type has to be a valid qualified name. Not sure if one is a subset of the other.
  But overall I think it's worth just having a dedicated field for the admissionCheck statuses.
  
  That also avoids the external controllers to concatenate an "AdmissionCheck" prefix into their condition name.

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:161** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-08-04T18:09:05Z

+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, each
+reflecting the go/no-go decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry CheckFailureState = “Retry”
+	Reject CheckFailureState = “Reject”
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check.
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+// Points to where the parameters for the checks are. 
+// As clusterqueue are in cluster scope - this should be
+// a dedicated CRD specific for the Controller.
+type AdmissionCheckParametersReference struct {
+	// ApiGroup is the group for the resource being referenced. 
+	APIGroup string `json:"apiGroup"`
+
+	// Kind is the type of the resource being referenced.
+	Kind string `json:"kind""`
+
+	// Name is the name of the resource being referenced.
+	Name string `json:"name"`
+}
+```
+
+For every workload that is put to a ClusterQueue, Kueue will perform the very 
+same checks that it does today, before admitting a workload. However, once the basic checks pass AND there are some AdmissionChecks configured, AND the workload is not in on-hold retry state from some check, it will:
+
+1. Fill the Admission field in workload, with the desired flavor assignment. 
+2. Not do any preemptions yet.
+3. Set conditions on the workload:
+* “AdmissionPrecheck” to true
+* “AdmissionCheck|<checkName>” to unknown for each of the add
+
+Kueue will only pass as many pods past AdmissionPrecheck as there would
+fit in the quota together, possibly limited by a Kueue configuration option.
+That would violate a bit BestEffort logic of queues - if there is 1000 tasks
+in a queue that doesn’t pass quota and 1001st task passes, the best effort
+queue would let it in. BestEffort queue with 1000 tasks that don’t pass
+AdditioanlChecks would not let 1001st task in (it will not reach the
```

  ```suggestion
  admissionChecks would not let 1001st task in (it will not reach the
  ```

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:221** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-08-04T18:13:03Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,226 @@
+# KEP-993: Two Stage Admission Process
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)](#notesconstraintscaveats-optional)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP defines the extension point to plug in arbitrary, additional checks
+for workloads before they are admitted for execution. These external checks may
+be implemented inside or outside of Kueue and may provide functionality like
+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.
+
+## Motivation
+
+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, each
+reflecting the go/no-go decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry CheckFailureState = “Retry”
+	Reject CheckFailureState = “Reject”
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check.
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+// Points to where the parameters for the checks are. 
+// As clusterqueue are in cluster scope - this should be
+// a dedicated CRD specific for the Controller.
+type AdmissionCheckParametersReference struct {
+	// ApiGroup is the group for the resource being referenced. 
+	APIGroup string `json:"apiGroup"`
+
+	// Kind is the type of the resource being referenced.
+	Kind string `json:"kind""`
+
+	// Name is the name of the resource being referenced.
+	Name string `json:"name"`
+}
+```
+
+For every workload that is put to a ClusterQueue, Kueue will perform the very 
+same checks that it does today, before admitting a workload. However, once the basic checks pass AND there are some AdmissionChecks configured, AND the workload is not in on-hold retry state from some check, it will:
+
+1. Fill the Admission field in workload, with the desired flavor assignment. 
+2. Not do any preemptions yet.
+3. Set conditions on the workload:
+* “AdmissionPrecheck” to true
+* “AdmissionCheck|<checkName>” to unknown for each of the add
+
+Kueue will only pass as many pods past AdmissionPrecheck as there would
+fit in the quota together, possibly limited by a Kueue configuration option.
+That would violate a bit BestEffort logic of queues - if there is 1000 tasks
+in a queue that doesn’t pass quota and 1001st task passes, the best effort
+queue would let it in. BestEffort queue with 1000 tasks that don’t pass
+AdditioanlChecks would not let 1001st task in (it will not reach the
+checks). Without this limitation, a large number of tasks could be switched
+back and forth from Precheck to suspended state. 
```

  When we have determined that checks for a workload don't pass (and the retry period is over), we should probably put the workload in the `inadmissibleWorkloads` set.
  This way, BestEffort would mostly work the same way as before, except that it's, potentially, slower.

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:161** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-08-04T18:22:18Z

+## Summary

+suspended state.

+
+## Proposal

+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, each
+reflecting the go/no-go decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry CheckFailureState = “Retry”
+	Reject CheckFailureState = “Reject”
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check.
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+// Points to where the parameters for the checks are. 
+// As clusterqueue are in cluster scope - this should be
+// a dedicated CRD specific for the Controller.
+type AdmissionCheckParametersReference struct {
+	// ApiGroup is the group for the resource being referenced. 
+	APIGroup string `json:"apiGroup"`
+
+	// Kind is the type of the resource being referenced.
+	Kind string `json:"kind""`
+
+	// Name is the name of the resource being referenced.
+	Name string `json:"name"`
+}
+```
+
+For every workload that is put to a ClusterQueue, Kueue will perform the very 
+same checks that it does today, before admitting a workload. However, once the basic checks pass AND there are some AdmissionChecks configured, AND the workload is not in on-hold retry state from some check, it will:
+
+1. Fill the Admission field in workload, with the desired flavor assignment. 
+2. Not do any preemptions yet.
```

  This one is tricky. Let's take the scenario of ProvisioningRequest.
  
  If a Workload requires preemptions to fit and we don't do preemptions, the ProvisioningRequest would likely trigger a scale up or fail because it reached the scale up limits (or reached stockout).
  
  OTOH, if we do the preemptions, and the ProvisioningRequest cannot be satisfied for whatever reason, we would have done preemptions for nothing (or too early). Not sure if this should be a configuration parameter for the check.
  
  Another open question: if we defer preemptions, should any more workloads be admitted in the cohort while waiting for the admissionChecks? In general I think we should not. Or perhaps it should be per flavor/resource that needs preemption or is borrowing, like in #1036.

### Review by [@trasc](https://github.com/trasc) (commented) — 2023-08-07T10:07:54Z

```

  +1 for this being tricky, and also not very easy to do with the current preemption mechanism.
  On the overall two steps admission, I propose, as a first stage to not change the way the preemption is done.
  
  In the future, maybe we can add a built in `AdmissionCheckPreempt`, the controller of which should be in charge of issuing evictions and wait for the resources to become available.

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:154** by [@trasc](https://github.com/trasc) — 2023-08-07T10:07:42Z

+for workloads before they are admitted for execution. These external checks may

+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.

+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.

+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.

+suspended state.

+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted.

+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, each
+reflecting the go/no-go decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry CheckFailureState = “Retry”
+	Reject CheckFailureState = “Reject”
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check.
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+// Points to where the parameters for the checks are. 
+// As clusterqueue are in cluster scope - this should be
+// a dedicated CRD specific for the Controller.
+type AdmissionCheckParametersReference struct {
+	// ApiGroup is the group for the resource being referenced. 
+	APIGroup string `json:"apiGroup"`
+
+	// Kind is the type of the resource being referenced.
+	Kind string `json:"kind""`
+
+	// Name is the name of the resource being referenced.
+	Name string `json:"name"`
+}
+```
+
+For every workload that is put to a ClusterQueue, Kueue will perform the very 
+same checks that it does today, before admitting a workload. However, once the basic checks pass AND there are some AdmissionChecks configured, AND the workload is not in on-hold retry state from some check, it will:
+
+1. Fill the Admission field in workload, with the desired flavor assignment. 
+2. Not do any preemptions yet.
+3. Set conditions on the workload:
+* “AdmissionPrecheck” to true
+* “AdmissionCheck|<checkName>” to unknown for each of the add
```

  Maybe it makes sense to have list checks populated and maintained throughout the entire life of the workload, this way the check controller can choose if it wants to wait for the kueue admission to be set before it updates it's specific status.

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2023-08-07T20:20:10Z

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:102** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-08-07T20:20:09Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,226 @@
+# KEP-993: Two Stage Admission Process
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)](#notesconstraintscaveats-optional)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP defines the extension point to plug in arbitrary, additional checks
+for workloads before they are admitted for execution. These external checks may
+be implemented inside or outside of Kueue and may provide functionality like
+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.
+
+## Motivation
+
+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, each
+reflecting the go/no-go decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
```

  Done

+* “AdmissionCheck|<checkName>” to unknown for each of the add
+
+Kueue will only pass as many pods past AdmissionPrecheck as there would
+fit in the quota together, possibly limited by a Kueue configuration option.
+That would violate a bit BestEffort logic of queues - if there is 1000 tasks
+in a queue that doesn’t pass quota and 1001st task passes, the best effort
+queue would let it in. BestEffort queue with 1000 tasks that don’t pass
+AdditioanlChecks would not let 1001st task in (it will not reach the
```

+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry CheckFailureState = “Retry”
+	Reject CheckFailureState = “Reject”
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check.
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+// Points to where the parameters for the checks are. 
+// As clusterqueue are in cluster scope - this should be
+// a dedicated CRD specific for the Controller.
+type AdmissionCheckParametersReference struct {
+	// ApiGroup is the group for the resource being referenced. 
+	APIGroup string `json:"apiGroup"`
+
+	// Kind is the type of the resource being referenced.
+	Kind string `json:"kind""`
+
+	// Name is the name of the resource being referenced.
+	Name string `json:"name"`
+}
+```
+
+For every workload that is put to a ClusterQueue, Kueue will perform the very 
+same checks that it does today, before admitting a workload. However, once the basic checks pass AND there are some AdmissionChecks configured, AND the workload is not in on-hold retry state from some check, it will:
+
+1. Fill the Admission field in workload, with the desired flavor assignment. 
+2. Not do any preemptions yet.
+3. Set conditions on the workload:
+* “AdmissionPrecheck” to true
+* “AdmissionCheck|<checkName>” to unknown for each of the add
```

  Ok, added.

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2023-08-07T21:15:19Z

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:161** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-08-07T21:15:19Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,226 @@
+# KEP-993: Two Stage Admission Process
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)](#notesconstraintscaveats-optional)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP defines the extension point to plug in arbitrary, additional checks
+for workloads before they are admitted for execution. These external checks may
+be implemented inside or outside of Kueue and may provide functionality like
+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.
+
+## Motivation
+
+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, each
+reflecting the go/no-go decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry CheckFailureState = “Retry”
+	Reject CheckFailureState = “Reject”
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check.
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+// Points to where the parameters for the checks are. 
+// As clusterqueue are in cluster scope - this should be
+// a dedicated CRD specific for the Controller.
+type AdmissionCheckParametersReference struct {
+	// ApiGroup is the group for the resource being referenced. 
+	APIGroup string `json:"apiGroup"`
+
+	// Kind is the type of the resource being referenced.
+	Kind string `json:"kind""`
+
+	// Name is the name of the resource being referenced.
+	Name string `json:"name"`
+}
+```
+
+For every workload that is put to a ClusterQueue, Kueue will perform the very 
+same checks that it does today, before admitting a workload. However, once the basic checks pass AND there are some AdmissionChecks configured, AND the workload is not in on-hold retry state from some check, it will:
+
+1. Fill the Admission field in workload, with the desired flavor assignment. 
+2. Not do any preemptions yet.
```

  We cannot start with preemptions - if we preempt we will create a "hole" in in the quota and the preempted workload will try to get in again immediately. Thus preemption can only work with simultaneous admission or other form of the resource reservation. Thus if we preeempt, we should account the precheckedWorkloads in the quota, that basically means that we cannot have best effort queues as we have right now, only "moderate effort" ;).

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2023-08-09T09:17:20Z

+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]

+	// to admit a workload.  
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"addotomalChecks"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry CheckFailureState = “Retry”
+	Reject CheckFailureState = “Reject”
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check.
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+// Points to where the parameters for the checks are. 
+// As clusterqueue are in cluster scope - this should be
+// a dedicated CRD specific for the Controller.
+type AdmissionCheckParametersReference struct {
+	// ApiGroup is the group for the resource being referenced. 
+	APIGroup string `json:"apiGroup"`
+
+	// Kind is the type of the resource being referenced.
+	Kind string `json:"kind""`
+
+	// Name is the name of the resource being referenced.
+	Name string `json:"name"`
+}
+```
+
+For every workload that is put to a ClusterQueue, Kueue will perform the very 
+same checks that it does today, before admitting a workload. However, once the basic checks pass AND there are some AdmissionChecks configured, AND the workload is not in on-hold retry state from some check, it will:
+
+1. Fill the Admission field in workload, with the desired flavor assignment. 
+2. Not do any preemptions yet.
```

  In general, we probably need 3 modes of operations:
  
  * Preempt after checks pass - for checks that are not fully correlated with quota, and can take a longer time to give a green light.
  * Preempt before checks are started - for checks that are essentially yet another quota check.
  * Mix of the two based on the status provided by the check. The check may say:
     * Preempt now, as i'm hitting quota issues and preemption may help
     * Preempt after I give a green light, no quota issues observed at this moment and the admission will take a longer time, so there is no need to stop the running workloads yet. 
  
  I will update the document to reflect that.

### Review by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) (commented) — 2023-08-11T19:32:56Z

@@ -0,0 +1,246 @@
+# KEP-993: Two Stage Admission Process
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)

+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)

+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP defines the extension point to plug in arbitrary, additional checks
+for workloads before they are admitted for execution. These external checks may
+be implemented inside or outside of Kueue and may provide functionality like
+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.
+
+## Motivation
+
+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, 
+in a dedicated field in the status, each reflecting the go/no-go 
+decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload. The order of the checks doesn't matter,
+	// all of them will be started at the same time.
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"admissionChecks"`
+}
+
+// WorkloadStatus defines the observed state of Workload
+type WorkloadStatus struct {
+[...]
+	// Status of admission checks, if there are any specified 
+	// for the ClusterQueue in which the workload is queued.
+	AdmissionChecksStatuses []metav1.Condition `json:"admissionChecksStatuses,omitempty"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry metav1.ConditionStatus = “Retry”
+	Reject metav1.ConditionStatus = “Reject”
+	QuotaExhausted metav1.ConditionStatus = "QuotaExhausted"
+)
```

  nit, move before `AdmissionChecksStatuses`, so that it's more clear that it's about them (IIUC).
  
  But in general, explain what they mean.

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:144** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-08-11T19:19:16Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,246 @@
+# KEP-993: Two Stage Admission Process
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)](#notesconstraintscaveats-optional)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP defines the extension point to plug in arbitrary, additional checks
+for workloads before they are admitted for execution. These external checks may
+be implemented inside or outside of Kueue and may provide functionality like
+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.
+
+## Motivation
+
+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, 
+in a dedicated field in the status, each reflecting the go/no-go 
+decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload. The order of the checks doesn't matter,
+	// all of them will be started at the same time.
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"admissionChecks"`
+}
+
+// WorkloadStatus defines the observed state of Workload
+type WorkloadStatus struct {
+[...]
+	// Status of admission checks, if there are any specified 
+	// for the ClusterQueue in which the workload is queued.
+	AdmissionChecksStatuses []metav1.Condition `json:"admissionChecksStatuses,omitempty"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry metav1.ConditionStatus = “Retry”
+	Reject metav1.ConditionStatus = “Reject”
+	QuotaExhausted metav1.ConditionStatus = "QuotaExhausted"
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check (after it transitioned to False).
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+
+	// If set to true, the workload will preempt other and block
+	// capacity before the check is passed.
+	BookCapacity bool `json:"bookCapacity,omitempty"`
```

  ```suggestion
  	BookQuota bool `json:"bookQuota,omitempty"`
  ```

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:165** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-08-11T19:20:27Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,246 @@
+# KEP-993: Two Stage Admission Process
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)](#notesconstraintscaveats-optional)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP defines the extension point to plug in arbitrary, additional checks
+for workloads before they are admitted for execution. These external checks may
+be implemented inside or outside of Kueue and may provide functionality like
+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.
+
+## Motivation
+
+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, 
+in a dedicated field in the status, each reflecting the go/no-go 
+decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload. The order of the checks doesn't matter,
+	// all of them will be started at the same time.
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"admissionChecks"`
+}
+
+// WorkloadStatus defines the observed state of Workload
+type WorkloadStatus struct {
+[...]
+	// Status of admission checks, if there are any specified 
+	// for the ClusterQueue in which the workload is queued.
+	AdmissionChecksStatuses []metav1.Condition `json:"admissionChecksStatuses,omitempty"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry metav1.ConditionStatus = “Retry”
+	Reject metav1.ConditionStatus = “Reject”
+	QuotaExhausted metav1.ConditionStatus = "QuotaExhausted"
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check (after it transitioned to False).
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+
+	// If set to true, the workload will preempt other and block
+	// capacity before the check is passed.
+	BookCapacity bool `json:"bookCapacity,omitempty"`
+}
+
+// Points to where the parameters for the checks are. 
+// As clusterqueue are in cluster scope - this should be
+// a dedicated CRD specific for the Controller.
+type AdmissionCheckParametersReference struct {
+	// ApiGroup is the group for the resource being referenced. 
+	APIGroup string `json:"apiGroup"`
+
+	// Kind is the type of the resource being referenced.
+	Kind string `json:"kind""`
+
+	// Name is the name of the resource being referenced.
+	Name string `json:"name"`
+}
+```
+
+For every workload that is put to a ClusterQueue that has admissionChecks
+configured Kueue will add admissionCheckStatuses:
+
+* “AdmissionPrecheck” to false
```

  ```suggestion
  * “AdmissionPrecheck” in `status.conditions` to false
  ```

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:158** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-08-11T19:22:32Z

@@ -0,0 +1,246 @@
+# KEP-993: Two Stage Admission Process

+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)

+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.
+
+## Motivation
+
+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, 
+in a dedicated field in the status, each reflecting the go/no-go 
+decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload. The order of the checks doesn't matter,
+	// all of them will be started at the same time.
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"admissionChecks"`
+}
+
+// WorkloadStatus defines the observed state of Workload
+type WorkloadStatus struct {
+[...]
+	// Status of admission checks, if there are any specified 
+	// for the ClusterQueue in which the workload is queued.
+	AdmissionChecksStatuses []metav1.Condition `json:"admissionChecksStatuses,omitempty"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry metav1.ConditionStatus = “Retry”
+	Reject metav1.ConditionStatus = “Reject”
+	QuotaExhausted metav1.ConditionStatus = "QuotaExhausted"
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check (after it transitioned to False).
```

  When this time is over, would we transition back to Unknown? That could be a good signal to requeue.

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:226** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-08-11T19:27:10Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,246 @@
+# KEP-993: Two Stage Admission Process
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)](#notesconstraintscaveats-optional)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+      - [Prerequisite testing updates](#prerequisite-testing-updates)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP defines the extension point to plug in arbitrary, additional checks
+for workloads before they are admitted for execution. These external checks may
+be implemented inside or outside of Kueue and may provide functionality like
+budgeting, capacity provisioning or some elements of multicluster dispatching.
+
+## Motivation
+
+With the growth of Kueue, not all desired elements may land inside of the core
+Kueue. Some users may even not want to publish their custom admission logic in
+a public repository. At the same time, we don’t want to force users to
+fork Kueue. Thus, an pluggable mechanism for workload admission needs to
+be established.
+
+### Goals
+
+Define mechanism to allow external controllers:
+
+* to give green light to admit a workload.
+* to temporarily hold workload admission.
+* to stop a previously admitted workload and move it back to the
+suspended state.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+Provide a specific design or implementation for any external controller.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Extend ClusterQueue definition with a list of external controller names that
+need to give green light to admit a workload. Until all of the controllers, which
+identify with these names, don’t give a green light, the workload will not
+be admitted. 
+
+Each workload that goes to such a queue, will get additional conditions, 
+in a dedicated field in the status, each reflecting the go/no-go 
+decision of each of the external controllers. Once
+a controller is confident that the workload can be admitted, it flips the
+status of the corresponding condition from false to true. 
+
+If a controller changes its mind about a workload, it can switch the condition
+back to false and the workload will be immediately suspended.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to use the [Cluster Autoscaler ProvisioningRequest API](https://github.com/kubernetes/autoscaler/pull/5848) 
+to ensure that the resources can be provided in full before starting the workload.  
+
+#### Story 2
+
+I want to base workload admission on budget. I have the actual consumption metrics
+in my Prometheus/Datadog/Stackdriver/whatever monitoring system. And weekly
+budget in a CRD, per namespace. I’m happy to modify some small existing sample
+controller, but I don’t want to fork the whole Kueue to adjust some minor details.
+ 
+### Notes/Constraints/Caveats (Optional)
+
+Each of the go/no-go decisions is best-effort and can be reversed at any time. 
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+## Design Details
+
+We will extend ClusterQueueSpec definition by adding a reference to
+AdmissionChecks that the queue needs to perform before admitting a
+workload. The design of AdmissionChecks is similar to IngressClass
+- it allows passing additional parameters, specific to particular checks
+that need to be performed. 
+
+```
+// ClusterQueueSpec defines the desired state of ClusterQueue
+type ClusterQueueSpec struct {
+[...]
+	// List of AdmissionCheck names that needs to be passed
+	// to admit a workload. The order of the checks doesn't matter,
+	// all of them will be started at the same time.
+	AdmissionChecks []string `json:"admissionChecks"`
+}
+
+// WorkloadStatus defines the observed state of Workload
+type WorkloadStatus struct {
+[...]
+	// Status of admission checks, if there are any specified 
+	// for the ClusterQueue in which the workload is queued.
+	AdmissionChecksStatuses []metav1.Condition `json:"admissionChecksStatuses,omitempty"`
+}
+
+
+// Cluster-scoped top-level object defining a check that 
+// can be referenced in ClusterQueue
+type AdmissionCheck struct {
+	metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+	metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+	Spec AdmissionCheckSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+	Retry metav1.ConditionStatus = “Retry”
+	Reject metav1.ConditionStatus = “Reject”
+	QuotaExhausted metav1.ConditionStatus = "QuotaExhausted"
+)
+
+type AdmissionCheckSpec struct {
+// Name of the controller which will actually perform
+// the checks. Cannot be empty.
+	ControllerName string `json:"controllerName"`
+
+	// How long to keep the workload suspended 
+	// after a failed check (after it transitioned to False).
+	RetryDelayMinutes *int64. `json:"retryDelayMinutes,omitempty"`
+
+	// A reference to the additional parameters for the check. 
+	Parameters *AdmissionCheckParametersReference `json:"parameters,omitempty"`
+
+	// If set to true, the workload will preempt other and block
+	// capacity before the check is passed.
+	BookCapacity bool `json:"bookCapacity,omitempty"`
+}
+
+// Points to where the parameters for the checks are. 
+// As clusterqueue are in cluster scope - this should be
+// a dedicated CRD specific for the Controller.
+type AdmissionCheckParametersReference struct {
+	// ApiGroup is the group for the resource being referenced. 
+	APIGroup string `json:"apiGroup"`
+
+	// Kind is the type of the resource being referenced.
+	Kind string `json:"kind""`
+
+	// Name is the name of the resource being referenced.
+	Name string `json:"name"`
+}
+```
+
+For every workload that is put to a ClusterQueue that has admissionChecks
+configured Kueue will add admissionCheckStatuses:
+
+* “AdmissionPrecheck” to false
+* “<checkName>” to unknown for each of the AdmissionChecks
+
+Kueue will perform the very same checks that it does today, 
+before admitting a workload. However, oncethe basic checks 
+pass AND there are some AdmissionChecks configured, AND the
+workload is not in on-hold retry state from some check, it will:
+
+1. Fill the Admission field in workload, with the desired flavor assignment. 
+2. Not do any preemptions yet (unless BookCapacity is set to true).
+3. Set “AdmissionPrecheck” admisisonChecksStatuses  to true.
+
+Kueue will only pass as many pods past AdmissionPrecheck as there would
+fit in the quota together, possibly limited by a Kueue configuration option.
+That would violate a bit BestEffort logic of queues - if there is 1000 tasks
+in a queue that doesn’t pass quota and 1001st task passes, the best effort
+queue would let it in. BestEffort queue with 1000 tasks that don’t pass
+AdmissionChecks would not let 1001st task in (it will not reach the
+checks). Without this limitation, a large number of tasks could be switched
+back and forth from Precheck to suspended state. 
+
+
+Then it will wait until all additional check conditions are satisfied (set
+to true). Once it happens, the Kueue will recheck that Admission settings
+are still valid (check quota/preemptions/reclamation) and admit the
+workload (doing preemptions if needed). Kueue will also recheck all of the
+prechecked workloads on every other workload admission, to make sure
+that their flavor admission is still possible. 
+
+If any of these checks fails (either on the final check or when admission
+other workloads), the workload gets back to the suspended state, and gets
+their AdmissionChecks and AdmissionPrecheck cleared.
+
+If any check is switched to Reject or Retry, the workload is either
```

  Completely rejected means that we will mark the Job as failed?

- **keps/993-two-phase-admission/README.md:228** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-08-11T19:29:41Z
